## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity), which matches second-order ODE models for harmonic and nonlinear oscillators. Common structures express dv_dt as a sum of restoring forces depending on x, damping terms depending on v, and possible external/time-dependent forcing depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (Hooke restoring force): dv_dt = c0 * x (linear small-amplitude regime, sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator with linear drag)
- Quadratic (speed) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (turbulent/pressure drag-like damping in oscillators)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sign(v) (stick-slip/friction-dominated oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- General odd restoring-force polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (symmetric potential with higher-order stiffness)
- Van der Pol oscillator (nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations / limit cycles)
- Rayleigh oscillator (nonlinear damping in v): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (self-excited oscillations with velocity-dependent pumping)
- Driven damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic forcing near resonance)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance, jump phenomena)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type stiffness modulation): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (parametric resonance via time-varying stiffness)
- Potential-gradient form (conservative + damping + forcing): dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3) + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (interpretable as -dU/dx plus damping/drive)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative (energy-preserving) oscillator structure → dv_dt depends on x only (no v term); often an odd function of x for symmetric potentials (e.g., x, x**3, x**5).
- Linear damping → additive term proportional to v; trajectories spiral toward equilibrium in phase space when forcing is absent.
- Nonlinear damping that changes sign with amplitude → factors like (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v create self-excitation at small amplitude and dissipation at large amplitude, yielding a limit cycle.
- Hardening/softening stiffness → inclusion of x**3 (and higher odd powers) shifts effective frequency with amplitude (backbone curve behavior).
- Dry friction signatures → dv_dt includes sign(v) (or smooth approximations like tanh(c*v)); leads to piecewise-smooth dynamics and possible sticking.
- Quadratic drag regime → v*Abs(v) term; dissipation grows faster with speed and can strongly attenuate large-velocity portions of motion.
- External periodic forcing → explicit sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms; enables resonance, entrainment, and steady-state oscillations even with damping.
- Parametric excitation → time-periodic modulation multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x); produces instability tongues (Mathieu-type behavior) near twice the natural frequency.
- Symmetry breaking or biased equilibrium → presence of even powers of x (e.g., x**2) or constant offsets in dv_dt indicates asymmetric potentials or constant external fields.

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed):
\[
F(t,x,v)=0.719321236251799\sin t\;-\;0.0856781567252997\,v^3\;-\;1.91960248272986\,v\;-\;1.73029531320599\,x\,(0.0808213006269486\,t+1)
\]
So GT contains exactly these structural pieces:
- a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (no exponential envelope),
- a \(v^3\) term,
- a linear \(v\) term,
- an \(x\) term with a coefficient affine in \(t\): \(-Kx(\gamma t+1)=-(K\gamma)\,t\,x -Kx\).
No other dependence (no \(x^3\), no \(|v|\), no \(\exp(\cdot)\) dependence multiplying \(v\) or the trig, etc.).

Below, “can match” means: there exists a choice of the candidate constants making the candidate identically equal to GT for all real \(x,t,v\).

### 1.
\(c0 x + c1 e^{c2 t}\sin(c3 t+c4)+ c5 v e^{c6 t}+ c7\sin(c8 t+c9)\)

- GT has no \(v e^{(\cdot)t}\) term; to remove it set \(c7=0\).
- Remaining: \(c0 x + c1 e^{c2 t}\sin(c3 t+c4)+ c5 v^3 + c6 v\).

- Can set \(c2=0\), and combine sine/cos into a single sine with phase by choosing one of them zero (e.g., \(c7=0\)) or matching \(0.7193\sin t\) via phase shift.
- Can match \(v^3\) and \(v\).
- Still cannot generate the \(t x\) cross-term.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO37)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.0856781567252997*v**3 - 1.91960248272986*v - 1.73029531320599*x*(0.0808213006269486*t + 1) + 0.719321236251799*sin(t)`

Expanding: `-0.0856781567252997*v**3 - 1.91960248272986*v - 0.139836708...*x*t - 1.73029531320599*x + 0.719321236251799*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v**3` (coefficient ≈ -0.0857)
2. `v` (coefficient ≈ -1.9196)
3. `x*t` (coefficient ≈ -0.1398)
4. `x` (coefficient ≈ -1.7303)
5. `sin(t)` (coefficient ≈ 0.7193)

Now I need to check which candidates can reproduce ALL these terms exactly.

**Key observations about candidates:**
- Most candidates contain `c1*exp(c2*t)*sin(c3*t + c4)`. Setting c2=0 gives `c1*sin(c3*t + c4)`, which can match `sin(t)` with c3=1, c4=0. ✓
- Many contain `c5*v*exp(c6*t)`. This gives `v*exp(c6*t)`, which is NOT equivalent to `v**3 + v` or `v + x*t`. Setting c6=0 gives just `c5*v`. This provides the `v` term but NOT `v**3`.
- The `x*t` term is crucial and unusual. None of the candidates explicitly have `x*t`.

Let me check if any candidate can produce `x*t`:
- `c0*x` gives `x` only
- No candidate has an explicit `x*t` term

**Can `exp(c2*t)*sin(c3*t+c4)` produce both `sin(t)` and `x*t`?** No, it's independent of x.

**Can any combination produce `x*t`?** Looking at candidates with `x*cos(c*t)` (Candidates 3, 13): `x*cos(c*t)` is NOT `x*t`.

None of the candidates have an `x*t` term. The GT requires `x*t` as a basis function. Since `x*t` is linearly independent from all basis functions present in the candidates (x, x³, x⁵, v, v³, sin(t), cos(t), exp(ct)*sin(...), v*exp(ct), etc.), no candidate can match.

Wait - let me reconsider. Could `x*cos(c*t)` approximate `x*t`? No, by Rule 2, no approximations allowed.

Could `v*exp(c*t)` somehow combine with other terms? No, v and x are independent variables.

Let me verify there's truly no candidate with `x*t`. Scanning all 50 candidates... None have `x*t` explicitly.

The only way to get `x*t` would be from a product of x-dependent and t-dependent terms. Candidates like `c8*x*cos(c9*t)` (Candidates 3, 13) give `x*cos(ct)` which is NOT `x*t` for any constant choice.

Since `x*t` is a required basis function in the GT and is linearly independent from all basis functions available in every candidate, **no candidate can match**.
